## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Mechanical Engineering - Plasticity/Viscoelasticity
**Analysis**: This task likely belongs to the domain of plasticity/viscoelasticity, as it involves the relationship between stress, strain, and temperature in materials. The task may model the nonlinear stress-strain behavior of materials under different temperatures.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Ramberg-Osgood relation: sigma = epsilon + c0 * epsilon**(c1) (nonlinear stress-strain behavior)
- Friedrich model: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) (nonlinear viscoelastic stress-strain relationship)
- Kelvin-Voigt model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * exp(-c2 * t) (time-dependent viscoelastic stress-strain behavior)
- Mooney-Rivlin equation: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (strain-energy function for incompressible elastomers)
- Bergstrom-Boyce model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear viscoelastic stress-strain relationship)
- Adiabatic shear band model: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) + c2 * epsilon * exp(-c3 * t) (thermomechanical shear band formation)
- Linear isotropic hardening model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * sigma_y (incremental plasticity model with isotropic hardening)
- Norton's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (creep model for metallic materials)
- Exponential stress-strain relation: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) (nonlinear stress-strain behavior)
- Power-law stress-strain relation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**(c1) (nonlinear stress-strain behavior)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal activation effects → exponential functions exp(c*x), exp(-c*x)
- Rate-dependent effects → multiplicative factors of time-dependent functions, eg, exp(-c*t) or t**c
- Nonlinear hardening/softening → polynomial or rational functions in strain epsilon
- Thermal sensitivity → multiplicative factors of temperature T or its functions
- Viscoelastic/viscoplastic behavior → stress-strain relations with time-dependent components
